يطهر حينئذ إلا بالغسل لعدم الملجيء كما قيل . وقيل : ولو بال ولم ينتشر البول على رأس الذكر بأن لم يتجاوز الثقب فأمنى لا يحكم بتنجيس المني، وكذا إذا جاوز لكن خرج المني دفقاً من غير أن ينتشر على رأس الذكر لأنه لم يوجد سوى مروره على البول في مجراه ولا أثر لذلك في الباطن .ا.هـ. وظاهر المتون الإطلاق أعني سواء بال واستنجى أو لم يستنج بالماء فإن المني يطهر بالفرك لأنه مغلوب مستهلك كالمذي، ولم يعف في المذي إلا لكونه مستهلكاً لا لأجل الضرورة. وأطلق في الثوب فشمل الجديد والغسيل فيطهر كلا منهما بالفرك، وقيده في غاية البيان بكون الثوب غسيلاً احترازاً عن الجديد فإنه لا يطهر بالفرك ولم أره فيما عندي من الكتب لغيره وهو بعيد كما لا يخفى. وشمل ما إذا كان للثوب بطانة نفذ إليها وفيه اختلاف، والصحيح أن البطانة تطهر بالفرك كالظاهرة لأنه من أجزاء المني. كذا في النهاية وغيرها. ثم نجاسة المني عندنا مغلظة. كذا في السراج الوهاج معزياً إلى خزانة الفقيه أبي الليث. وحقيقة الفرك الحك باليد حتى يتفتت كذا في شرح ابن الملك. وقد صرح المصنف بطهارة المحل بالفرك، وكذا في الكل وفيه اختلاف نذكره في آخرها إن شاء الله تعالى. وفي المجتبى وبقاء أثر المني بعد الفرك لا يضر كبقائه بعد الغسل. وفي المسعودي : مني الإنسان نجس وكذا مني كل حيوان وأشار إلى أن العلقة والمضغة نجسان كالمني، وقد صرح بذلك في النهاية ،والتبيين وكذا الولد إذا لم يستهل فهو نجس ولهذا قال قاضيخان في فتاواه ؛ الولد إذا نزل من المرأة ولم يستهل وسقط في الماء أفسده، سواء غسل أو لا. وكذا لو حمله المصلي لا تصح صلاته .اهـ. وفي المجتبى : أصاب الثوب دم عبيط فيبس فحته طهر الثوب كالمني اهـ. وفيه نظر لتصريحهم بأن طهارة الثوب بالفرك إنما هو في المني لا في غيره. وفي البدائع : وأما سائر النجاسات إذا أصابت الثوب أو البدن ونحوهما فإنها لا تزول إلا بالغسل، سواء كانت رطبة أو يابسة، وسواء كانت سائلة أو لها جرم. ولو أصاب ثوبه خمر فألقى عليها الملح ومضى عليه من المدة مقدار ما يتخلل فيها لم يحكم بطهارته حتى يغسله، ولو أصابه عصير فمضى عليه من المدة مقدار ما يتخمر العصير لا يحكم بنجاسته اهـ .
It becomes pure then except by washing due to absence of necessity as it is said. And it is said: If he urinated and the urine did not spread on the tip of the penis, i.e. it did not exceed the opening, and then he emitted semen, it is not ruled that the semen is impure. Similarly, if it exceeded but the semen came out in a gush without spreading on the tip of the penis, because nothing occurred except its passage over urine in its channel, and there is no effect of that in the interior. End quote. And the apparent meaning of the texts is absolute, i.e. whether he urinated and performed istinja or did not perform istinja with water, indeed the semen is purified by rubbing because it is overwhelmed and consumed like madhi. And madhi is excused only because it is consumed, not due to necessity. And he made it absolute regarding the garment, including new and washed; both are purified by rubbing. But in Ghayat al-Bayan it was restricted to a washed garment to exclude a new one, for it is not purified by rubbing. I have not seen it in any of my books from others, and it is far-fetched as is not hidden. And it includes when the garment has a lining and [the semen] penetrated it; there is a difference of opinion. The correct view is that the lining is purified by rubbing like the outer layer because it is part of the semen. So it is in al-Nihayah and others. Then, the impurity of semen with us is severe. So it is in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, attributed to Khizanat al-Faqih Abi al-Layth. The reality of rubbing is scraping with the hand until it crumbles, so it is in Sharh Ibn al-Malik. And the author explicitly stated the purification of the spot by rubbing, and similarly in all, and there is a difference of opinion which we will mention at its end if Allah wills. In al-Mujtaba: The remaining trace of semen after rubbing does not harm, like its remaining after washing. In al-Mas'udi: Human semen is impure, and similarly the semen of every animal. And he indicated that the 'alaqah and mudghah are impure like semen. And it is explicitly stated in al-Nihayah and al-Tabyin, and similarly a child who has not cried [at birth] is impure. For this reason Qadikhan said in his Fatawa: If a child descends from a woman and does not cry and falls into water, he spoils it, whether washed or not. Similarly, if a praying person carries him, his prayer is not valid. End quote. In al-Mujtaba: If a garment is affected by fresh blood and it dries, then it is scraped off, the garment becomes pure like semen. End quote. And there is consideration in it because of their explicit statement that purification of the garment by rubbing is only in semen, not in others. In al-Bada'i: As for all other impurities, if they affect a garment or body or the like, they are not removed except by washing, whether wet or dry, whether liquid or solid. And if a garment is affected by wine and he puts salt on it and time passes enough for it to become vinegar, it is not ruled pure until he washes it. And if it is affected by juice and time passes enough for the juice to become wine, it is not ruled impure. End quote.
Source pages p. 390

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses the purification of semen (mani) from garments. It is an intra-Hanafi dispute, discussing the ruling that semen is purified by rubbing (fark) without washing, unlike other impurities. The passage begins by noting a previous condition where semen is not ruled impure if urine did not spread. The author clarifies that the general ruling is that semen is purified by rubbing because it is 'consumed' (mustahlak) in the fabric, similar to madhi (pre-ejaculate fluid). Madhi is excused due to consumption, not necessity. The author criticizes a restriction in Ghayat al-Bayan that only washed garments are purified by rubbing, calling it far-fetched. The ruling includes new garments and even linings if semen penetrates, though there is ikhtilaf; the correct view is that the lining is purified like the outer layer. Semen is considered a severe impurity but is unique in being purified by rubbing. The passage then compares with other impurities: blood scraping is analogous to semen but rejected; other najasat require washing. Wine and juice are discussed: adding salt to wine does not purify it until washed; juice becomes impure only if it actually becomes wine. The passage ends with a note that all other impurities require washing.

Key Terms
المني (al-mani): Semen, which is considered a severe impurity (najis maghlazah) in the Hanafi school.
الفرك (al-fark): Rubbing or scraping the garment with the hand until the dry impurity crumbles and falls off.
المستهلك (al-mustahlak): Consumed or overwhelmed in the fabric, such that no trace remains visible or separable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how is semen (mani) purified from a garment?
A) By washing with water three times
B) By rubbing (fark) until it crumbles and falls off
C) By applying salt and waiting
D) By sprinkling water once

Key Takeaway
The unique Hanafi ruling that semen is purified by rubbing is based on consumption (istihlak) and does not extend to other impurities.

Taharah — Purification

Purification of Smooth Objects by Wiping: Hanafi Ruling and Intra-Madhhab Dispute
Explains ruling that smooth, non-porous objects are purified by wiping, not washing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on purifying smooth objects by wiping, identify the conditions and exceptions, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on the nature of the purification.

Core Idea
A smooth, non-porous object is purified by wiping alone, based on the Companions' practice; the trace must be removed.

The Hanafi school uniquely allows purification of smooth, non-porous objects by wiping (mas'h) rather than washing. This ruling is derived from the practice of the Companions after battle. However, there is a dispute within the school on whether wiping effects true purification (taharah haqiqiyyah) or merely makes the object excused (taharah hukmiyyah) for use, which has practical implications for items cut with a wiped knife.

Guided Path
1
Identify the object and its characteristics
Determine if the object is smooth (saqil) and non-porous (la masam lah). Examples include swords, glass, metal plates, fingernails, bone, ebony, and unengraved gold/silver sheets.
Porous objects (e.g., cloth, wood with pores) require washing.
2
State the ruling and its condition
The object is purified by a single wipe. However, the trace of impurity (athar) must be removed. If the trace remains, wiping is insufficient.
Wiping can be done with any dry material (dirt, rag, wool).
3
Recognize exceptions
Objects with pores, rust, or engraving are not purified by wiping. They require washing with water. Also, smooth garments have pores and thus need washing.
The presence of pores (masam) prevents purification by wiping.
4
Understand the proof
The proof is the practice of the Companions who wiped their swords after killing disbelievers and then prayed with them. This indicates the Prophet's tacit approval.
The proof has zanni thubut and dalalah.
5
Distinguish the intra-Hanafi dispute
Some Hanafi scholars hold that wiping effects true purification (taharah haqiqiyyah), while others say it only makes the object excused (taharah hukmiyyah). The practical difference: if a knife wiped from najasah cuts food, it is halal to eat according to the first view, but not the second. The mufta bihi is the first (true purification) with the condition of trace removal.
Al-Karkhi's view is chosen for fatwa, as per al-Inayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

He made it absolute, so it includes wet and dry, stool and urine. And it is mentioned in al-Asl that urine and blood are not purified except by washing, and wet stool likewise, and dry stool is purified by scraping according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) contrary to Muhammad (al-Shaybani). So it is in al-Inayah. And the author indicated its purification by wiping like its analogs, and there is difference in it: some say it becomes pure in reality, some say it is only excused, and to this points the statement of al-Quduri when he said: 'He sufficed with wiping them' and did not say 'they become pure'. The correct view will be mentioned later. And in its analogs, the benefit is that if one cuts watermelon or meat with a knife that has been wiped from impurity, it is permissible to eat it according to the first view, not the second. And it is not hidden that wiping is only purifying on condition that the trace is removed, as Qadikhan restricted it in his Fatawa. There is no difference whether he wipes it with dirt, a rag, sheep's wool, or other, as in the Fatawa also. And 'masam' are the pores of a thing.
Source pages p. 390

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses the purification of smooth, non-porous objects (like swords) by wiping (mas'h). It is an intra-Hanafi dispute and also touches on the proof from the Companions' practice. The author explains that any solid, smooth object without pores is purified by a single wipe, whether new or old. Exceptions are new swords with rust or engraving (require washing), and smooth garments (have pores). Included are fingernails, glass, oiled bowls, turned wood, reed mats, bone, ebony, and unengraved gold/silver plates. The basis is the practice of the Companions who wiped their swords after battle and prayed with them, and the principle that impurity does not penetrate such surfaces. There is a difference on whether wiping effects true purification (tabir) or merely makes it excused; al-Quduri's wording suggests the latter. The practical difference: cutting food with a wiped knife—if true purification, the food is halal; if mere excuse, it is not. The author notes that wiping must remove the trace of impurity, and the material used for wiping (dirt, rag, wool) does not matter. Urine and blood require washing on non-smooth surfaces, but on smooth objects, wiping suffices.

Key Terms
المسح (al-mas'h): Wiping or passing a dry material over the surface of a smooth object to remove impurity.
الجسم الصقيل (al-jism al-saqil): A smooth, polished object without pores, such as a sword, glass, or metal plate.
المسام (al-masam): Pores or openings in a surface that allow penetration of impurity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Smooth, non-porous objects are purified by wiping with trace removal, based on the Companions' practice; the intra-Hanafi dispute on the nature of purification does not affect the mufta bihi ruling.

Purification of Earth by Drying: Prayer Valid but Tayammum Invalid
Ruling with proof: purification of earth by drying

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on purified earth by drying and explain why drying restores taharah but not tahuriyyah.

Core Idea
Dried earth is pure for prayer, not tayammum, because tahuriyyah is not restored.

In this lesson, we examine a key Hanafi ruling regarding contaminated earth that becomes dry. The text from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq establishes that such earth is pure for prayer but cannot be used for tayammum because it lacks the quality of being purifying (tahuriyyah). Understanding the distinction between taharah (purity) and tahuriyyah (purifying capacity) is essential for correctly applying this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State the dual outcome: earth becomes pure for prayer by drying, but remains invalid for tayammum.
The ruling is conditional on the disappearance of the trace of impurity.
2
Locate the proof
The text cites the athar of A'ishah and Muhammad ibn al-Hanafiyyah: 'Zakat of the earth is its dryness.' This is interpreted as a proof for restoration of purity.
This is a qawl sahabi, considered zanni in transmission and meaning.
3
Understand the legal reasoning
Before contamination, earth was both tahir and tahur. Contamination removed both. Drying legally restores only taharah, not tahuriyyah. Therefore tayammum is invalid.
The author prefers this explanation over the specification-based reasoning of other commentators.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The passage implies a difference with other schools on whether drying restores all qualities; the Hanafi position is that it does not.
This difference is rooted in how general texts are handled in usul al-fiqh.
5
Apply the ruling
The mufta bihi position: prayer is valid on dried contaminated earth, but tayammum is not. A person in need of tayammum must find a tahur surface.
This affects daily practice for those praying on outdoor ground or in situations of impurity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله ( والأرض باليبس وذهاب الأثر للصلاة لا للتيمم أي تطهر الأرض المتنجسة بالجفاف إذا ذهب أثر النجاسة فتجوز الصلاة عليها، ولا يجوز التيمم منها لأثر عائشة ومحمد ابن الحنفية : زكاة الأرض يبسها أي طهارتها. وإنما لم يجز التيمم منها لأن الصعيد علم قبل التنجس طاهراً وطهوراً وبالتنجس علم زوال الوصفين، ثم ثبت بالجفاف شرعاً أحدهما أعني الطهارة فيبقى الآخر على ما علم من زواله وإذا لم يكن طهوراً لا يتيمم به، وهذا أولى مما ذكره الشارحون في الفرق بأن طهارة المكان ثبتت بدلالة النص التي خص منها حالة غير الصلاة، والنجاسة القليلة والعام المخصوص من الحجج المجوّزة كخبر الواحد فجاز تخصيصه بالأثر بخلاف قوله تعالى فتيمموا فإنه من الحجج الموجبة التي لم يدخله تخصيص، في الشرع النطفة نجسة ثم تصير علقة وهي نجسة وتصير مضغة فتطهر قوله : (والخشب الخراطي) بفتح الخاء المعجمة والراء المشددة بعدها ألف وكسر الطاء المهملة آخره ياء مشددة نسبة إلى الخراط، وهو خشب يخرطه الخراط فيصير صقيلاً كالمرآة. قوله : (والبوريا) الحصير المنسوج قاموس. قوله : (فإن المصنف في الكافي قال بعده الخ) قال في الكفاية : ويمكن أن يجاب عنه بأن المراد بالعموم الإطلاق وأنه يثبت الحكم في جميع الأفراد أيضاً، وكذا المراد بالتخصيص التقييد يعني ما لا يمكن الاحتراز عنه عند الشافعي وأكثر من قدر الدرهم عندنا فيكون مؤوّلاً فيعارضه خبر الواحد.
His statement: (And the earth by drying and disappearance of the trace for prayer not for tayammum) i.e., the impure earth is purified by drying when the trace of impurity disappears, so prayer on it is permissible, but tayammum from it is not permissible, due to the athar of A'ishah and Muhammad ibn al-Hanafiyyah: 'The purification of the earth is its dryness' i.e., its purity. And the reason why tayammum is not permissible from it is that the soil was known before contamination to be pure and purifying, and with contamination it was known that both characteristics were removed. Then by drying, legally one of them is established, namely purity, so the other remains as known to have been removed. When it is not purifying, one does not perform tayammum with it. This is better than what the commentators mentioned as the difference: that the purity of the place is established by the indication of the text which was specified from the case other than prayer, and minor impurity, and a general text that is specified is among the permissible proofs like khabar al-wahid, so it is permissible to specify it by the trace, contrary to His statement 'so perform tayammum' (Quran), for it is among the obligatory proofs that have not been subject to specification. In the law, the nutfah is impure, then becomes 'alaqah and it is impure, then becomes mudghah and becomes pure. His statement: (And turned wood) ... (and buraya) the woven mat, lexicon. His statement: (Indeed, the author in al-Kafi said after it, etc.) He said in al-Kifayah: It can be answered that what is meant by 'general' is absolute, and that the ruling is established in all individuals as well. Similarly, what is meant by specification is restriction, meaning what cannot be avoided according to al-Shafi'i, and more than the measure of a dirham according to us, so it is interpreted and thus contradicts khabar al-wahid.
Source pages p. 391

Commentary
This passage addresses the purification of earth by drying (yubs). It is a ruling with proof. The author states that contaminated earth becomes pure for prayer when the impurity dries and its trace disappears, but it cannot be used for tayammum. The proof is from the athar of A'ishah and Muhammad ibn al-Hanafiyyah: 'The purification of the earth is its dryness.' The reasoning: before contamination, earth was both tahir (pure) and tahur (purifying). Contamination removed both. Drying legally restores only taharah, not tahuriyyah. Therefore, it is pure for prayer but not for tayammum. The author prefers this explanation over the one given by other commentators who rely on specification of general texts. The passage then digresses into definitions of 'turned wood' and 'buraya' from the previous lesson on smooth objects, and a discussion on specification of general proofs versus khabar al-wahid, which seems to be a response to an objection. The final part compares rulings on nutfah stages.

Key Terms
اليبس (al-yubs): Drying of the earth such that the trace of impurity disappears.
الصعيد (al-sa'id): The surface of the earth; in tayammum, it must be tahur (purifying).

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) It becomes pure only after a rain

Key Takeaway
Dry earth is pure for prayer but not for tayammum because drying restores only taharah, not tahuriyyah.

Taharah — Purification

Purification of Earth and Fixed Surfaces by Drying
Expands the ruling on purification by drying

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on purification by drying for earth and fixed surfaces, and distinguish which objects are purified by drying versus those requiring washing.

Core Idea
Earth and its fixed attachments are purified by drying; cut or movable objects require washing.

Impurity on the ground can be removed by simply waiting for it to dry—this is the Hanafi position. But not every surface shares this ruling. In this lesson, we explore which surfaces are purified by drying (jafaf) and which require washing, based on the detailed commentary of Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
Recognize that the passage establishes that earth (and things fixed to it) become pure by drying. This is the relied-upon (mukhtar) position in the Hanafi school.
The word 'mukhtar' indicates the preferred view for fatwa.
2
Understand the interpretive dispute
Examine the disagreement over the meaning of 'al-tayyib' (pure vs. plant-growing land). Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i restrict purification to plant-growing land, but the Hanafi position takes 'al-tayyib' as pure earth, thus all earth is purified by drying.
The argument uses usul: specification (takhsis) requires prior generality, which is not present here.
3
List objects that share the ruling
Identify that walls, trees, grass, reeds, gypsum, and fixed bricks are included as long as they remain fixed in the earth. Cut wood, reeds, and movable bricks are excluded.
The ruling hinges on whether the object is 'fixed' (thabit) in the earth.
4
Apply conditions for valid purification
Drying must result in removal of all traces (taste, color, smell). The method of drying (sun, fire, wind, shade) does not matter. If the impurity is wet, washing is required first.
Al-Quduri restricted drying to the sun, but the text removes that restriction as custom-based.
5
Distinguish special cases: stone and brick
Smooth stones require washing; absorbent stones (like millstones) are like earth. Movable bricks are not purified by drying, but fixed bricks can be if they dry before being lifted.
The passage cites multiple authorities (al-Khujandi, al-Sayrafi, al-Nihaya) showing a nuanced view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المشترك لا فإن المصنف في الكافي قال بعده: ولي فيه إشكال لأن النص لا عموم له في الأحوال لأنها غير داخلة تحت النص وإنما تثبت ضرورة والتخصيص يستدعي سبق التعميم، ولأن الطيب يحتمل الطاهر والمنبت . وعلى الثاني حمله أبو يوسف والشافعي ولا يجوز أن يكونا مرادين لأن وهو من الحجج المجوّزة كالعام المخصوص قيد بالأرض له فيكون مؤوّلاً، عموم احترازاً عن الثوب والحصير والبدن وغير ذلك فإنها لا تظهر بالجفاف مطلقاً. ويشارك الأرض في حكمها كل ما كان ثابتاً فيها كالحيطان والأشجار والكلأ والقصب وغيره ما دام قائماً عليها، فيطهر بالجفاف وهو المختار. كذا في الخلاصة. فإن قطع الخشب والقصب وأصابته نجاسة فإنه لا يطهر إلا بالغسل. ويدخل في القصب الخص بضم الخاء المعجمة وبالصاد المهملة البيت من القصب والمراد به هنا السترة التي تكون على السطوح من القصب. كذا في شرح الوقاية وكذا الجص بالجيم كما في الخلاصة حكمه حكم الأرض بخلاف اللبن الموضوع على الأرض. وأما الحجر فذكر الخجندي أنه لا يطهر بالجفاف. وقال الصيرفي : إن كان الحجر أملس فلا بد من الغسل، وإن كان تشرب النجاسة كحجر الرحا فهو كالأرض والحصى بمنزلة الأرض. وأما اللبن والآجر فإن كانا موضوعين ينقلان ويحولان فإنهما لا يطهران بالجفاف لأنهما ليسا بأرض وإن كان اللبن مفروشاً فجف قبل أن يقلع طهر بمنزلة الحيطان. وفي النهاية : إن كانت الآجرة مفروشة في الأرض فحكمها حكم الأرض، وإن كانت موضوعة تنقل وتحوّل، فإن كانت النجاسة على الجانب الذي يلي الأرض جازت الصلاة عليها، وإن كانت النجاسة على الجانب الذي قام عليه المصلي لا تجوز صلاته . في السراج الوهاج. وإذا رفع الآجر عن الفرش هل يعود نجساً؟ فيه روايتان كذا البزازية وسيأتي بيان الصحيح في نظائرة. كذا في وأطلق في اليبس ولم يقيده بالشمس كما قيده القدوري لأن التقييد به مبني على العادة وإلا فلا فرق بين الجفاف بالشمس والنار والريح والظل. وقيد باليبس لأن النجاسة لو كانت رطبة لا تطهر إلا بالغسل، فإن كانت رخوة تتشرب الماء كما صب عليها فإنه يصب عليها الماء حتى يغلب على ظنه أنها طهرت، ولا توقيت في ذلك . وعن أبي يوسف يصب بحيث لو كانت هذه النجاسة في الثوب طهر، واستحسن هذا صاحب الذخيرة. وإن كانت صلبة إن كانت منحدرة حفر في أسفلها حفيرة وصب عليها الماء، فإذا اجتمع في تلك الحفيرة كبسها أعني الحفيرة التي فيها الغسالة وإن كانت صلبة مستوية فلا يمكن الغسل بل يحفر ليجعل أعلاه في أسفله وأسفله في أعلاه، وإن كانت الأرض مخصصة قال في الواقعات : يصب عليها الماء ثم يدلكها وينشفها بخرقة أو صوفة ثلاثاً فتطهر جعل ذلك بمنزلة غسل الثوب في الإجانة والتنشيف بمنزلة العصر، فإن لم يفعل ذلك ولكن صب عليها الماء كثيراً حتى زالت النجاسة ولم يوجد لها لون ولا ريح ثم تركها حتى نشفت طهرت كذا في السراج الوهاج والخلاصة والمحيط . وقيد بذهاب الأثر الذي هو الطعم واللون والريح لأنها لو جفت وذهب أثرها بالرؤية وكان إذا وضع أنفه شم الرائحة لم تجز الصلاة على مكانها. كذا في السراج الوهاج. وفي الفتاوى إذا احترقت الأرض بالنار فتيمم بذلك التراب؛ قيل يجوز التيمم، وقيل لا يجوز، والأصح الجواز.
The common [word] is not... For the author in al-Kafi said after it: I have an issue with it because the text does not have generality in states, because they are not included under the text, but are established by necessity, and specification requires prior generality. And because 'al-tayyib' can mean pure and also that which grows plants. Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i carried it on the second meaning, and it is not possible that both are intended because it is among the permissible proofs like a general text restricted to earth, so it becomes interpreted. [It is] a generality to exclude garment, mat, body and other things, for they do not become pure by drying at all. And everything that is fixed in the earth like walls, trees, grass, reeds, and other things as long as they are standing on it shares the ruling of earth, so it becomes pure by drying, and that is the chosen position. Thus in al-Khulasa. If wood and reeds are cut and najasah befalls them, they do not become pure except by washing. And included in reeds is 'al-khus' – with damm on the khā' and ṣād – the house of reeds, and what is meant here is the screen on roofs made of reeds. Thus in Sharh al-Wiqaya. Likewise, gypsum with jīm, as in al-Khulasa, its ruling is the ruling of earth, unlike bricks placed on earth. As for stone, al-Khujandi mentioned that it does not become pure by drying. And al-Sayrafi said: If the stone is smooth, washing is necessary; if it absorbs the najasah like a millstone, it is like earth, and pebbles are in the position of earth. As for bricks and baked bricks, if they are placed such that they are moved and transferred, they do not become pure by drying because they are not earth. If the brick is laid and dries before being lifted, it becomes pure like walls. In al-Nihaya: If the baked brick is laid in the earth, its ruling is the ruling of earth; if it is placed such that it is moved and transferred, if the najasah is on the side facing the earth, prayer on it is permissible; if the najasah is on the side on which the worshipper stands, his prayer is not permissible. In al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. If the brick is lifted from its bedding, does it become najis again? There are two narrations, thus in al-Bazzaziyya, and the explanation of the correct one will come in its parallels. Thus in and he said generally about dryness and did not restrict it to the sun as al-Quduri restricted it, because the restriction is based on custom, otherwise there is no difference between drying by sun, fire, wind, and shade. And he restricted it by dryness because if the najasah is wet, it does not become pure except by washing. If it is soft and absorbs water like water poured on it, then water is poured on it until he is predominantly sure it has become pure, and there is no time limit for that. From Abu Yusuf: He pours such that if this najasah were on a garment, it would become pure, and the author of al-Dhakhira approved this. If it is solid: if it is sloping, a pit is dug at its bottom and water is poured on it. When it collects in that pit, he presses it – meaning the pit containing the washing water. If it is solid and level, washing is not possible; rather, he digs to make its top become its bottom and its bottom its top. If the earth is designated [for washing], al-Waqi'at says: He pours water on it, then rubs it and dries it with a cloth or wool three times, so it becomes pure. He made that like washing a garment in a basin, and drying like wringing. If he does not do that, but pours much water on it until the najasah is gone and no color or smell remains, then leaves it until it dries, it becomes pure. Thus in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, al-Khulasa, and al-Muhit. And it is conditioned by the removal of trace, which is taste, color, and smell, because if it dries and its trace is gone by sight, but if he puts his nose he smells the odor, prayer on that place is not permissible. Thus in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. And in al-Fatawa: If the earth is burned by fire and one makes tayammum with that dust, it was said tayammum is permissible, and it was said it is not permissible, and the most correct is permissibility.
Source pages p. 392

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, deals with the purification of earth and fixed surfaces by drying (jafaf). It is an 'expansion probe' that clarifies the ruling and its conditions. The passage begins by addressing an interpretative issue: the word 'al-tayyib' (often translated as 'good' or 'pure') in the primary text can mean either pure earth or earth that grows plants. Abu Yusuf and Imam al-Shafi'i interpreted it as the latter, but the Hanafi position restricts the ruling to earth itself, arguing that the specification to earth prevents generality. The author then states the relied-upon (mukhtar) ruling: earth and everything fixed in it—such as walls, trees, grass, and reeds while still standing—becomes pure by drying. However, cut wood or reeds require washing. The text then details various surfaces: gypsum and fixed bricks share earth's ruling; movable bricks and stones do not. For stones, there is a distinction between smooth ones (need washing) and absorbent ones (like earth). For bricks, if laid and dried before lifting, they purify by drying. The passage also addresses the method of washing both soft and solid earth: for soft earth, water is poured until the impurity is removed; for solid earth, digging, rubbing, and drying are prescribed. Importantly, drying is not restricted to sun; any means (fire, wind, shade) suffices. The condition for purification is the removal of all traces—taste, color, and smell. The passage ends with a minor ruling on tayammum with burnt earth, where the correct view is permissibility.

Key Terms
الجفاف (al-jafaf): The process by which the impurity dries up, leading to purification of earth and fixed surfaces.
الأرض (al-ard): The ground, including its fixed attachments (walls, trees, etc.), which can be purified by drying as long as they remain in place.
الطيب (al-tayyib): A term that can mean either pure (tahir) or land that grows plants (munbit). In this context, the Hanafi position interprets it as pure earth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position in this passage, which of the following becomes pure by drying (jafaf)?
A) A cut piece of wood that falls on the ground
B) A wall made of bricks that is fixed in the earth
C) A garment that has dried after being washed
D) A stone that does not absorb water

Key Takeaway
Earth and its fixed attachments are purified by drying; cut or movable objects require washing, and all traces of impurity must be gone.

Return of Impurity After Non-Liquid Purification: The Two Narrations
Intra-Hanafi dispute on return of impurity after non-liquid purification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi narrations on the return of impurity after non-liquid purification and apply them to specific cases such as mani, khuff, earth, hide, and well.

Core Idea
Two narrations within the Hanafi school: impurity returns or not; the chosen view in later works often favors non-return.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents an intra-Hanafi dispute: if a surface purified by rubbing, drying, or tanning becomes wet, does impurity return? Understanding this ikhtilaf requires careful attention to the specific cases and the authorities who supported each view. The passage serves as a documentation of the differing transmissions within the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
Recognize the question: when a surface has been purified by a non-liquid method (e.g., rubbing, drying, tanning), and later water touches it, does the original impurity return? The passage reports two narrations (riwayatan).
The issue only arises because liquid water is not used initially; the purification is considered valid but may be incomplete.
2
Understand the two narrations
The first narration holds that impurity returns because the impurity was only reduced (qallat) but not entirely eliminated (lam tazul). The second holds that it does not return because the purification is complete once the trace is gone.
The more apparent view according to al-Zayla'i is that impurity returns, but many later authorities favor non-return.
3
Survey the five specific cases
List the five cases: (1) mani on a garment after rubbing, (2) leather sock (khuff) after rubbing, (3) earth after drying and trace removal, (4) hide of a dead animal after legal tanning, (5) a well when its water disappears and returns. For each, note the differing rulings among Hanafi authorities.
Additional cases mentioned: laid brick (ajur) and knife when wiped. These also fall under the two narrations.
4
Determine the preferred view
Examine Al-Khulasa, which frequently selects non-return as the chosen view (mukhtar) for mani, khuff, earth, and brick. However, authorities like Qadikhan and Al-Haddadi sometimes favor return. The passage does not give a single mufta bihi; it records the ikhtilaf.
For tanned hide, the matns (core texts) agree on purity via tanning, implying non-return despite two narrations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم أعلم أن ما حكم بطهارته بمطهر غير المائعات إذا أصابه ماء هل يعود نجساً؟ فذكر الشارح الزيلعي أن فيها روايتين، وأن أظهرهما أن النجاسة تعود بناء على أن النجاسة قلت ولم تزل وحكى خمس مسائل : المني إذا فرك، والخف إذا دلك، والأرض إذا جفت مع ذهاب الأثر، وجلد الميتة إذا دبغ دباغاً حكمياً بالتتريب والتشميس، والبئر إذا غار ماؤها ثم عاد وقد اختلف التصحيح في بعضها ولا بأس بسوق عباراتهم. فأما مسألة المني فقال قاضيخان في فتاواه والصحيح أنه يعود نجساً. وفي الخلاصة : المختار أنه لا يعود نجساً. وأما مسألة الخف فقال في الخلاصة: هو كالمني في الثوب يعني المختار عدم العود. وقال الحدادي في السراج الوهاج : الصحيح أنه يعود نجساً . وأما مسألة الأرض فقال قاضيخان في فتاواه : الصحيح أنها لا تعود نجسة. وقال في المجتبى : الصحيح عدم عود النجاسة وفي الخلاصة بعد ما ذكر أن المختار عدم نجاسة الثوب من المني إذا أصابه الماء بعد الفرك قال : وكذا الأرض على الرواية المشهورة. وأما مسألة جلد الميتة إذا دبغ ثم أصابه الماء فأفاد الشارح أنها على الروايتين لكن المتون مجمعة على الطهارة بالدباغ فإنهم يقولون : كل إهاب دبغ فقد طهر، وهو يقتضي عدم عودها. وأما مسألة البئر إذا غار ماؤها ثم عاد ففي الخلاصة : لا تعود نجسة وعزاه إلى الأصل. ويزاد على هذه الخمسة الآجرة المفروشة إذا تنجست فجفت ثم قلعت فعلى الروايتين وفي الخلاصة المختار عدم العود ويزاد السكين إذا مسحت فعلى الروايتين. وقال في السراج الوهاج : اختار القدوري عود النجاسة، واختار الأسبيجابي عدم العود وفي المحيط : الأرض إذا أصابتها النجاسة فيبست وذهب أثرها ثم أصابها الماء، والمني إذا فرك، والخف إذا دلك، متداخلاً في الأرض ..اهـ. قوله : (ثم تركها حتى نشفت طهرت) قال في الذخيرة بعد ذلك : وعند الحسن بن أبي مطيع قال : لو أن أرضاً أصابها نجاسة فصب عليها الماء فجرى عليها إلى أن أخذت قدر ذراع من الأرض طهرت الأرض والماء طاهر ويكون ذلك بمنزلة الماء الجاري. وفي المنتقى :
Then know that that which is ruled pure by a purifier other than liquids, if water touches it, does it return to being impure? Al-Sharih al-Zayla'i mentioned that there are two narrations, and the more apparent of them is that impurity returns, based on the fact that the impurity was little and did not cease. He narrated five cases: (1) mani when rubbed [from a garment], (2) the khuff when rubbed, (3) the earth when it dries with the removal of trace, (4) the skin of a dead animal when tanned a legal tanning by dusting and sunning, (5) the well when its water disappears then returns. And the verification differs in some of them, and there is no harm in citing their statements. As for the case of mani, Qadikhan said in his Fatawa: The correct [view] is that it returns to impurity. In al-Khulasa: The chosen view is that it does not return to impurity. As for the case of the khuff, in al-Khulasa: It is like mani on a garment, meaning the chosen view is non-return. Al-Haddadi said in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: The correct [view] is that it returns to impurity. As for the case of earth, Qadikhan said in his Fatawa: The correct [view] is that it does not return to impurity. In al-Mujtaba: The correct [view] is non-return of impurity. In al-Khulasa, after mentioning that the chosen view is that the garment does not become impure from mani when water touches it after rubbing, he said: Likewise earth according to the well-known narration. As for the case of the skin of a dead animal when tanned, then water touches it: the commentator informed that it is upon two narrations, but the matns are agreed on purity by tanning, for they say: Every hide that is tanned is pure, and that implies non-return. As for the case of the well when its water disappears then returns: in al-Khulasa, it does not return to impurity, and he attributed it to the original [books]. Added to these five is the laid baked brick: if it becomes impure and dries, then is lifted, it is upon two narrations, and in al-Khulasa the chosen view is non-return. Added also: the knife when wiped, it is upon two narrations. And in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: al-Quduri chose the return of impurity, and al-Uspijabi chose non-return. And in al-Muhit: The earth when impurity befalls it and it dries and its trace is gone, then water touches it; and mani when rubbed; and the khuff when rubbed; intermixing in the earth... Ends. His statement: (Then he leaves it until it dries, it becomes pure). Al-Dhakhira said after that: According to al-Hasan ibn Abi Muti', he said: If earth is affected by impurity and water is poured on it and flows over it until it takes a cubit's length of earth, the earth becomes pure and the water is pure, and that is like running water. And in al-Muntaqa:
Source pages p. 393

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a subtle but important issue in Hanafi fiqh: if a surface has been purified by a non-liquid method (e.g., drying, rubbing, tanning), and then later becomes wet, does the original impurity return? This is classified as an intra-Hanafi dispute. The commentator, al-Zayla'i, notes that there are two narrations (riwayatan) on this matter. The more apparent view is that impurity does return, because the impurity was merely reduced (qallat) but not completely eliminated. However, the author then lists five specific cases where the ruling is disputed: (1) semen on a garment after rubbing (fark); (2) leather sock (khuff) after rubbing; (3) earth after drying and removal of trace; (4) hide of a dead animal after legal tanning; (5) a well when its water returns after drying up. For each, he reports the opinions of later Hanafi authorities. Qadikhan favors the return of impurity for mani, while Al-Khulasa favors non-return. For the khuff, Al-Khulasa prefers non-return, but Al-Haddadi says the correct view is return. For earth, Qadikhan and Al-Mujtaba say non-return, with Al-Khulasa supporting that view as the well-known narration. For tanned hide, the matns (core texts) agree that tanning purifies, which implies non-return, but there are two narrations. For the well, Al-Khulasa says non-return. Additional cases are added: laid brick (ajur) if lifted after drying, and a knife when wiped—both have two narrations. The author also notes that al-Quduri and al-Uspijabi differed on the general principle. The passage ends with an additional note from Al-Dhakhira about washing earth with running water. The overall lesson: there is no single ruling; each case must be considered individually, and the later authorities (mutakhkhirin) differed.

Key Terms
المطهر غير المائعات (al-mutahhir ghayr al-mai'at): A purifier that is not a liquid, such as drying (jafaf), rubbing (fark), tanning (dibagh), or dusting/sunning.
الروايتان (al-riwayatan): Two transmitted narrations within the Hanafi school on the issue of whether impurity returns after non-liquid purification.
العود (al-'awd): The return of the original state of impurity after water touches a surface that had been purified by a non-liquid method.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school contains two narrations on the return of impurity after non-liquid purification; each case must be examined individually, and the later authorities often favor non-return.

Purification of Earth by Washing and Drying
Ruling on purifying earth by washing and drying

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two methods of purifying earth from najasah and identify the condition that must be met for the earth to be considered pure.

Core Idea
Earth becomes pure when all traces of impurity vanish—by washing and drying or by abundant water and natural drying.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling on purifying the ground after it has been contaminated with impurity. The passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq outlines two valid methods and emphasizes the critical condition of removing all perceptible traces. Understanding this will enable you to correctly determine when a surface is ritually pure for prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is purifying the earth (ground) after it becomes najis. The ruling is that with proper treatment, the earth becomes tahir (pure) and prayer upon it is valid.
2
List the conditions for purity
The essential condition is the removal of all three traces of the impurity: taste, color, and smell. If any trace remains, the ground remains najis.
3
Describe the two permissible methods
Method 1: Pour water, rub, and dry with a cloth three times (analogous to washing a garment and wringing). Method 2: Pour abundant water until the impurity and its traces are gone, then allow the ground to dry naturally.
For solid ground, if washing is not possible, one must dig and overturn the soil.
4
Apply the ruling to a scenario
If a dog urinates on a concrete courtyard, you must either scrub and dry it three times or flood it with water until no trace remains and leave it to dry. If after drying the smell persists, the spot remains impure.
5
Note the subsidiary ruling on burned earth
If the earth is burned by fire, it may be used for tayammum according to the soundest opinion.
This is an independent ruling related to taharah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كبسها أعني الحفيرة التي فيها الغسالة وإن كانت صلبة مستوية فلا يمكن الغسل بل يحفر ليجعل أعلاه في أسفله وأسفله في أعلاه، وإن كانت الأرض مخصصة قال في الواقعات : يصب عليها الماء ثم يدلكها وينشفها بخرقة أو صوفة ثلاثاً فتطهر جعل ذلك بمنزلة غسل الثوب في الإجانة والتنشيف بمنزلة العصر، فإن لم يفعل ذلك ولكن صب عليها الماء كثيراً حتى زالت النجاسة ولم يوجد لها لون ولا ريح ثم تركها حتى نشفت طهرت كذا في السراج الوهاج والخلاصة والمحيط . وقيد بذهاب الأثر الذي هو الطعم واللون والريح لأنها لو جفت وذهب أثرها بالرؤية وكان إذا وضع أنفه شم الرائحة لم تجز الصلاة على مكانها. كذا في السراج الوهاج. وفي الفتاوى إذا احترقت الأرض بالنار فتيمم بذلك التراب؛ قيل يجوز التيمم، وقيل لا يجوز، والأصح الجواز.
Press it, meaning the pit containing the wash water. If the ground is solid and level, washing is not possible; rather, one digs so that its top becomes bottom and bottom becomes top. If the ground is designated, it is stated in al-Waqi'at: He pours water on it, then rubs it and dries it with a cloth or wool three times, and it becomes pure. This is considered like washing a garment in a basin, and drying is considered like wringing. If he does not do that but pours a lot of water on it until the impurity is removed and no color or smell remains, then leaves it until it dries, it becomes pure. Thus in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, al-Khulasa, and al-Muhit. It is conditioned on the removal of the trace, which is taste, color, and smell, because if it dries and its trace disappears by sight, but if he puts his nose he smells the odor, prayer on that place is not valid. Thus in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. In al-Fatawa: If the earth is burned by fire and one performs tayammum with that soil; it is said that tayammum is permissible, and it is said that it is not permissible, and the soundest opinion is permissibility.
Source pages p. 393

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Hanafi school regarding the purification of earth contaminated with impurity. It describes two methods: (1) for solid ground, one must dig and overturn the soil; (2) for designated ground (e.g., a pit or courtyard), one pours water, rubs, and dries with a cloth three times—this is analogous to washing a garment and wringing it. Alternatively, if one pours abundant water until all traces of impurity vanish (color, taste, smell), then leaves it to dry, the earth becomes pure. The key condition is complete removal of the three traces. The passage also notes that if the earth was burned by fire (e.g., to sanitize it), the soil may be used for tayammum; the preferred view allows it.

Key Terms
الغسالة (al-ghasalah): The wash water that collects in a pit after washing impurity.
التجفيف (al-tajfif): Drying the ground after washing, considered analogous to wringing a garment.
الطعم واللون والريح (al-ta'm wa al-lawn wa al-rih): The taste, color, and smell of the impurity; their removal is a condition for the ground to become pure.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The ground must be dug up and overturned.

Key Takeaway
Earth becomes tahir for prayer only when all traces (taste, color, smell) of the najasah are removed, either by active washing and drying or by flooding and natural drying.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
8 min
The Seven Means of Purification and the Rule of Istihalah
Enumeration of purification methods and ruling on istihalah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the seven methods of purification in the Hanafi school, explain the concept of istihalah, and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding its purifying effect.

Core Idea
When a substance completely transforms into another species, impurity ceases.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq summarizes the seven recognized means of purification in the Hanafi school. While washing, rubbing, drying, wiping, and fire are familiar, the seventh—istihalah (transformation)—is a distinctive and debated principle. We will explore how a pig becoming salt or dung turning to ash can render a substance pure, and why some early Hanafi authorities differed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the seven methods
List the seven means of purification mentioned: washing, rubbing, drying, wiping on polished surfaces, wiping cupping cups, fire, and transformation.
The first four are common; transformation is the most jurisprudentially interesting.
2
Locate the ruling on transformation
Determine the hukm for each case: wine to vinegar (consensus), pig/dung to salt/ash (disputed). Note that the majority (Muhammad and Abu Hanifa) rule purity, while Abu Yusuf disagrees.
The passage explicitly states the fatwa is on Muhammad's view.
3
Trace the illa (effective cause)
The impurity is attached to the original reality (e.g., flesh, blood). When the substance changes entirely (e.g., to salt or ash), the reality ceases, so the ruling of impurity ceases. This is the basis of the qiyas (analogy).
The text uses examples from biology (nutfah to mudghah) and chemistry (juice to wine to vinegar) to illustrate that rulings follow the substance's essence.
4
Identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf held that transformation does not remove impurity; the original najasah remains. Muhammad and Abu Hanifa held that it does. The later scholars (e.g., al-Khulasa, Fath al-Qadir) chose Muhammad's view as the mufta bihi.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf among the early imams; the later tarjih is based on the strength of the dalil.
5
Evaluate the contradictory note on mudghah
The passage ends with a criticism: the author of al-Bahr earlier stated mudghah is impure, but later quoted Fath al-Qadir saying it is pure. The commentator leans toward impurity, creating a tension. This shows that istihalah's application to bodily stages is not fully settled.
This is an advanced point; not required for the basic ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم أعلم أنه قد ظهر إلى هنا أن التطهير يكون بأربعة أمور : بالغسل الدلك والجفاف والمسح في الصقيل دون ماء والفرك يدخل في الدلك والخامس مسح المحاجم بالماء بالخرق كما قدمناه. والسادس النار كما قدمناه في الأرض إذا احترقت بالنار. والسابع انقلاب العين فإن كان في الخمر فلا خلاف في الطهارة وإن كان في غيره كالخنزير والميتة تقع في المملحة فتصير ملحاً يؤكل . والسرقين والعذرة تحترق فتصير رماداً تطهر عند محمد خلافاً لأبي يوسف، وضم إلى محمد أبا حنيفة في المحيط، وكثير من المشايخ اختاروا قول محمد. وفي الخلاصة : وعليه الفتوى وفي فتح القدير أنه المختار لأن الشرع رتب وصف النجاسة على تلك الحقيقة وتنتفي الحقيقة بانتفاء بعض أجزاء مفهومها فكيف بالكل، فإن الملح غير العظم واللحم فإذا صار ملحاً ترتب حكم الملح ونظيره في الشرع النطفة نجسة وتصير علقة وهي نجسة وتصير مضغة فتطهر والعصير طاهر فيصير خمراً فينجس ويصير خلاً فيطهر، فعرفنا أن استحالة العين تستتبع زوال الوصف المرتب عليها وعلى قول محمد فرعوا الحكم بطهارة ... مخالف لما في مسألة فرك المني فتأمل. ثم رأيت بعض الفضلاء ذكر ما نصه : فيه نظر لما قدمنا أن العلقة والمضغة نجستان كالمني وقد صرح بذلك في النهاية والتبيين وقد تقدم ذلك عن البحر والعجب من صاحب البحر فإنه جزم هناك بأن المضغة نجسة ونقل هنا عن الفتح أنها طاهرة، وأقره وتبعه صاحب المنح في الموضعين ولم يتعقبه ولا يخفى ما في ذلك من التناقض. والظاهر أنها نجسة لتصريح النهاية والتبيين بذلك ولما تقدم في النفاس عن الخلاصة أن السقط إذا لم يستبن شيء من خلقه لا عبرة له وهو كالدم .اهـ. فإن المتبادر من غير المستبين الخلق أن يكون مضغة غير مخلقة وقد ذكر أن حكمها كالدم يعني أنها لم تخرج عن حقيقة الدم كالنطفة والعلقة وهما نجستان فتكون
Then know that it has become clear up to here that purification occurs by four things: by washing, rubbing, drying, and wiping on polished surfaces without water. Rubbing is included in rubbing. The fifth is wiping the cups of cupping with water and cloth as we have mentioned. The sixth is fire, as we mentioned regarding earth if it is burned by fire. The seventh is transformation of the substance. If it is wine, there is no disagreement on purity. If it is other than that, like a pig or a dead animal falling into a salt pit and becoming edible salt, or dung and feces burning and becoming ash, they become pure according to Muhammad, contrary to Abu Yusuf. In al-Muhit, Abu Hanifa is joined to Muhammad. Many scholars chose the opinion of Muhammad. In al-Khulasa: and upon it is the fatwa. In Fath al-Qadir, it is the chosen view because the Law assigned the description of impurity to that reality, and the reality ceases with the cessation of some parts of its concept, let alone all of it. For salt is not bone and flesh; so when it becomes salt, the ruling of salt applies. Its analogy in the Law: the sperm drop is impure, it becomes a clot which is impure, then it becomes a lump of flesh (mudghah) and becomes pure (according to some). Grape juice is pure, it becomes wine and becomes impure, then becomes vinegar and becomes pure. Thus we know that transformation of substance entails removal of the description attached to it. Based on Muhammad's opinion, they derived the ruling of purity... contrary to the issue of rubbing semen, so reflect. Then I saw some merit and honorable mention: There is consideration, because we have presented that the clot and the mudghah are both impure like semen, and it is explicitly stated in al-Nihayah and al-Tabyin. That has been mentioned earlier from al-Bahr. It is amazing from the author of al-Bahr that he affirmed there that the mudghah is impure, and he quoted here from al-Fath that it is pure, and he approved it, followed by the author of al-Munh in both places, and did not criticize it. The contradiction is not hidden. The apparent is that it is impure due to the explicit statements of al-Nihayah and al-Tabyin, and due to what was mentioned earlier in al-Nifas from al-Khulasa that a miscarriage if no part of its creation is apparent, it is disregarded and is like blood. The clear implication of 'not apparent in creation' is that it is a mudghah not yet formed, and its ruling is like blood, meaning it has not left the reality of blood, like the sperm and clot, both impure. So it would be...
Source pages p. 394

Commentary
This passage enumerates seven means of purification in the Hanafi school: (1) washing, (2) rubbing, (3) drying, (4) wiping on polished surfaces, (5) wiping cups of cupping with water and cloth, (6) fire, and (7) transformation of the substance (istihalah). The focus is on transformation. It is agreed that wine becoming vinegar is pure. For other transformations like a pig or dead animal turning into salt in a salt pit, or dung/feces burning to ash, there is a dispute: Muhammad al-Shaybani and Abu Hanifa (according to al-Muhit) rule that they become pure, while Abu Yusuf disagrees. The majority of later scholars follow Muhammad, and this is the basis for fatwa. The reasoning is that the ruling of impurity is attached to a specific reality (e.g., pig flesh), and when that reality is completely transformed into something else (salt, ash), the ruling ceases. Analogous examples from Islamic law: the sperm drop (nutfah) is impure, becomes a clot (alaqah) still impure, then becomes a lump of flesh (mudghah) which, according to some, becomes pure; grapes juice is pure, becomes wine which is impure, then becomes vinegar which is pure. This shows that istihalah removes impurity. However, the passage ends with a critical note about a contradiction: the author of al-Bahr had earlier stated that mudghah is impure, but then quoted from Fath al-Qadir that it is pure, creating an inconsistency. The commentator suggests that mudghah is impure based on other sources.

Key Terms
انقلاب العين (inqilab al-'ayn): The transformation of a substance into a different species, e.g., wine turning to vinegar, or pig flesh turning to salt.
الاستحالة (al-istihalah): Change of the essence of a substance, synonymous with inqilab al-'ayn.
المملحة (al-mamlahah): A salt pit or salt marsh where an impure animal falls and turns into salt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi position (Muhammad and Abu Hanifa), what happens when a dead animal falls into a salt pit and becomes salt?
A) The salt remains impure because the original impurity is still present.
B) The salt becomes pure because the substance has transformed.
C) The salt is pure only if it is washed three times.
D) The salt is impure only if it retains any color.

Key Takeaway
Complete transformation (istihalah) of a najis substance into a different species renders the new substance pure, a principle upheld by the majority of Hanafi scholars.

Taharah — Purification

Purification of Ground by Rain
Ruling on when rain purifies ground soiled by urine or feces

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition for purification of najis ground by rainwater and distinguish it from other views.

Core Idea
Rain purifies soil only when its water flows across the impurity.

This lesson examines a concise ruling from Ibn Nujaym's Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. The Hanafi school sets a specific condition for rainwater to purify ground soiled by urine or feces: the water must flow over the area. This distinguishes it from other schools that require mere contact. Understanding this condition is key when assessing the purity of a street after a light shower versus a heavy downpour.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what is being ruled upon: the purification of ground soiled by urine or feces through rain. The ruling is that such ground becomes pure when the condition is met.
The ruling is conditional, not absolute.
2
Identify the condition
The condition for purification is that the rain must be abundant enough that its water flows over the najis area. The key term is 'jara ma'uhu 'alayha' (its water flows over it).
Flow indicates sufficient quantity and force.
3
Apply the contrapositive
If the rain is little and does not flow, the ground does not become pure. This is explicitly stated: 'if the rain is little, its water does not flow over it, it is not purified.'
4
Compare with other schools
Note that the Shafi'i school holds that mere wetting is sufficient; the Hanafi requirement of flow is stricter.
This difference affects daily practice.
5
Derive the practical implication
In practice, after a light drizzle the ground remains impure; after a heavy downpour that creates runoff, it becomes pure.
Applied to streets, yards, and gardens.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أشار إلى أن أرض أصابها بول أو عذرة ثم أصابها المطر غالباً وقد جرى ماؤه عليها فذلك مطهر لها، وإن كان المطر قليلاً لم يجر ماؤه عليها لم تطهر اهـ.
He pointed out that ground which is struck by urine or feces, then rain strikes it predominantly and its water flows over it, that is a purifier for it. And if the rain is little, its water does not flow over it, it is not purified.
Source pages p. 394

Commentary
This is a ruling statement on the purification of najis ground by rainwater. The condition is that the rain must be so abundant that its water flows over the ground. If there is only a light rain that does not cause flow, the ground remains impure. This is the position of the Hanafi school as transmitted in the texts.

Key Terms
جرى ماؤه عليها (jara ma'uhu 'alayha): The rainwater flows over the najis ground, indicating sufficient quantity and force.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when does rain purify ground that has been soiled with urine?
A) Always, as long as rain touches it.
B) Only if the rain is heavy and its water flows over the area.
C) Only if it rains for a full day.
D) It never purifies; only water poured by hand purifies.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires rainwater to flow over najis ground for it to become pure; mere wetting is insufficient.
